    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12469737856293731365">Ellingham Academy is a famous private school in Vermont for the brightest thinkers, inventors, and artists. It was founded by Albert Ellingham, an early twentieth century tycoon, who wanted to make a wonderful place full of riddles, twisting pathways, and gardens. “A place,” he said, “where learning is a game.”<br/><br/>Shortly after the school opened, his wife and daughter were kid</span>
  <span id="freeText12469737856293731365" style="display:none">Ellingham Academy is a famous private school in Vermont for the brightest thinkers, inventors, and artists. It was founded by Albert Ellingham, an early twentieth century tycoon, who wanted to make a wonderful place full of riddles, twisting pathways, and gardens. “A place,” he said, “where learning is a game.”<br /><br />Shortly after the school opened, his wife and daughter were kidnapped. The only real clue was a mocking riddle listing methods of murder, signed with the frightening pseudonym “Truly, Devious.” It became one of the great unsolved crimes of American history.<br /><br />True-crime aficionado Stevie Bell is set to begin her first year at Ellingham Academy, and she has an ambitious plan: She will solve this cold case. That is, she will solve the case when she gets a grip on her demanding new school life and her housemates: the inventor, the novelist, the actor, the artist, and the jokester. But something strange is happening. Truly Devious makes a surprise return, and death revisits Ellingham Academy. The past has crawled out of its grave. Someone has gotten away with murder. <br /><br />The two interwoven mysteries of this first book in the Truly Devious series dovetail brilliantly, and Stevie Bell will continue her relentless quest for the murderers in books two and three.<br /><br /><strong><em>New York Times </em>bestselling author Maureen Johnson weaves a delicate tale of murder and mystery in the first book of a striking new series, perfect for fans of Agatha Christie and E. Lockhart.</strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="12469737856293731365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_2557650203" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2557650203" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2557650203?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2018-releases">2018-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-thriller-mystery">ya-thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep-side">lgbtq-rep-side</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-ff-side">lgbtq-ff-side</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2557650203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11986150698707736701"><strong>Me:</strong> *reads the last page and closes the book with a loud thump*<br/><br/><strong>Me, in a Buzzfeed Unsolved voice:</strong> with that in mind, let’s get into the THEORIES.<br/><br/>First of all, if I think about it hard enough, my physical form isn't even an objective fact of the universe and if I want the sequel to this book right now, I should have it.<br/><br/>Second of all, I still don't have the barest idea of who did it....but I suspect aliens were involved.<br/><br/><strong>
  <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br/><br/>At Ellingham Academy, Stephanie “Stevie” Bell fi</span>
  <span id="freeText11986150698707736701" style="display:none"><strong>Me:</strong> *reads the last page and closes the book with a loud thump*<br /><br /><strong>Me, in a Buzzfeed Unsolved voice:</strong> with that in mind, let’s get into the THEORIES.<br /><br />First of all, if I think about it hard enough, my physical form isn't even an objective fact of the universe and if I want the sequel to this book right now, I should have it.<br /><br />Second of all, I still don't have the barest idea of who did it....but I suspect aliens were involved.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br /><br />At Ellingham Academy, Stephanie “Stevie” Bell finds at last a scope to equal her abilities. Stevie is fascinated by crime and tends to throw herself at locked doors even when she’s sure they will never open. And there isn’t a more notorious locked door than the decades-old kidnapping and apparent murder of school founder and industrialist tycoon Albert Ellingham’s wife and daughter—a crime that exhaled enigma for years because of a malicious poem modeled in the style of Dorothy Parker that was signed “Truly, Devious” and sent to Mr. Ellingham. Stevie is all nerves and fascination and unabashedness and a deep, stirring hope: that, in Ellingham, she would be herself, apart from the watchful eyes of her conservative parents, and that she might solve the “Truly, Devious” crime and put the last specter of the past where it belongs.<br /><br />But while Stevie was exploring the school, mining for answers, tragedy strikes in the form of the murder of one of her housemates. Stevie is churned under by an overwhelming dread as her new reality sinks in: <strong>Truly Devious is back</strong>. Now, attending Ellingham Academy is starting to feel less like an opportunity and more as though Stevie's life had chased her down a dead-end corridor and trapped her there to taunt her.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>Schools may be famous for many things: academics, graduates, sports teams. They are not supposed to be famous for murders.</em>
  <br />
  <br />
</blockquote>Flipping the last page of this book felt like waking up and feeling the last tendrils of a dream melting away and leaving you there, in your bed, alone, stranded in the merciless intransigence of reality. I picked it up with no expectation at all, and it was like an unsuspected vault of delight spilling open. I couldn’t put it down. “<em>Just one more chapter</em>” became my mantra and the later at night it got, the further into another world I went.<br /><br /><em>Truly Devious</em> begins, as so many good stories do, with a <strong>murder</strong>. Then, it dives into a tightly engineered plot that zips along in short chapters entwining two different timelines—between 1936 and the present day. The author paces her twists very well and keeps you riveted with a slow-drip revelation of the real mindsets and motivations of her key characters. This is not the kind of novel where the author sets up the basic points of the plot early on, rather, Johnson turns up the heat so gradually that you don’t notice the water is boiling until it is too late. It’s the kind of novel that drives you into doubt, that keeps you wondering and fretting, stumbling behind its dancing feet. <br /><br />There’s an awful presentiment throughout the book that the pall of doom of the past had been leading to this moment. You know you’re missing crucial pieces of the puzzle and you’re trying to hold every word tight in your head, sifting it for meaning, but the book, ever so stubbornly, refuses to turn over its pockets for you. You keep reading, not because you want to reach the end, but because <strong>this book is just such a <em>pleasure</em> to read</strong>.<br /><br />The author deepens every delight with her engaging characters and the relationships between them occupy the bristling center. I loved Stevie. She is prone to trouble and any challenge, she would run to meet it. She is determined to solve the mystery and she spoke each word as if it were a stone she built her plans with. Her morbid fascination with crime is also so relatable (my hobbies include watching crime documentaries for an unhealthy amount of time and regretting it at night). Stevie also suffers from anxiety and is often plagued with panic attacks and that part was depicted so vividly that it felt so real.<br /><br />But this world wouldn’t be as fascinating if it was just Stevie soaking up the spotlight. Aside from her, we meet Stevie’s genius friend <strong>Janelle</strong> who’s black and a lesbian and her partner uses they/them pronouns, <strong>Nate</strong> who’s perpetually grumpy, has zero communication skills, is uncomfortable in every social situation, wears a shirt that says “IF YOU CAN READ THIS SHIRT, YOU ARE TOO CLOSE” and is therefore my spiritual animal, <strong>David</strong> who’s on that point on the spectrum of personality where “douchebag” becomes “nice guy” or “nice guy” becomes “douchebag” and I still don’t know how to feel about him, <strong>Hayes</strong> who’s a Youtube star with an online show about zombies and an unremarkably unpleasant attitude, and <strong>Ellie</strong> who seems like a cool person to hang out with but only for two hours at a time, otherwise you’ll probably end up being talked into committing a felony. Secondary characters include a Hijabi Muslim girl and a girl in a wheelchair and the casual diversity warmed the cold hollows of my heart.<br /><br />Overall, with a strong denouement and a deftly laid out ending that should segue well into the next installment, the author sets up the foundation for a very exciting sequel and I can't wait!<br /><br /><blockquote>✨ <a href="http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3" rel="nofollow noopener">wishlist</a> ✨ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ✨ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ✨</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="11986150698707736701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2283100338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2283100338" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2283100338?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2283100338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13346832165952204678">I LOVED THIS BOOK. If you need a new YA mystery novel, this is the one for you! <i>Truly Devious</i> totally took me by surprise. I had no idea I would love this book as much as I did! <br/><br/><br/>Cw: murder<br/><br/>I loved our main character, Stevie. I wish this book existed in high school so that I could have had a female protagonist interested in true crime to relate to. I feel Stevie is extremely competent, self-aware, and has a really great head on her shoulders. I also loved her best friends, Janelle – we need more b</span>
  <span id="freeText13346832165952204678" style="display:none">I LOVED THIS BOOK. If you need a new YA mystery novel, this is the one for you! <i>Truly Devious</i> totally took me by surprise. I had no idea I would love this book as much as I did! <br /><br /><br />Cw: murder<br /><br />I loved our main character, Stevie. I wish this book existed in high school so that I could have had a female protagonist interested in true crime to relate to. I feel Stevie is extremely competent, self-aware, and has a really great head on her shoulders. I also loved her best friends, Janelle – we need more black girls who like girls in STEM fields in media, and Nate – he’s such an apathetic lil bean who I hope gets more development in the sequel. I wasn’t a crazy big fan of David (I guess he is considered the love interest? <i>Truly Devious</i> is FAR from a heavy romance story, but there is definite attraction). He just sort of weirded me out; Motives unclear half the time, sometimes annoying, sometimes charming. I can’t really feel out his character at this point, but I did enjoy him more towards the ending and I’m hopeful he’ll grown on me more in the future.<br /><br />I am not a huge fan of dual timeline books where it jumps from present to past with a completely different set of characters, but it worked well for this book. The scenes set in 1936 do not overtake the present story, but are a great addition to the story. It does not feel “info-dumpy”, rather, it is like reading two mysteries unfolding at once.<br /><br />I adore the mystery of the story. You truly CANNOT TELL who is “Truly Devious”, if the same killer has returned, or else how these two crimes are really connected! There are so many twists and turns and unanswered questions that you will be on the edge of your seat trying to figure out how everything fits together.<br /><br />I will add, I do feel like the pacing was a bit slow at some points. There are not many significant plot points until about halfway through. That being said, I keep reminding myself that most thrillers are condensed into one book, whereas this will be a trilogy, so I understand the decision/need to have a more fleshed out beginning before diving into all the drama. I am anxiously anticipating book two and am extremely hopeful that things will be nonstop action from here.<br /><br /><i>Truly Devious</i> is truly amazing. It is a MUST READ. Book #2 is already going to the top of my most anticipated releases for 2019.<br /><br /><i> This book was sent to me unsolicited and for free by Harper Collins. I had no obligation to review this book and all opinions are my own.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13346832165952204678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2234665534" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2234665534" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2234665534?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2234665534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12609459725773879722"><b>HOLY FREAKING CLIFFHANGER</b>!!!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461697152ra/18898985.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I am actually happy I put off reading <i>Truly Devious</i> for almost a year after it was released, because honestly, I don't think I could have waited for the sequel.<br/><br/>Well played, Maureen Johnson. Well played!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484147672ra/21687118.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Ellingham Academy</i>, set in the remote mountains of Vermont, is a private school for gifted students, founded by the wealthy industrialist, Albert Ellingham, at the turn of the 20th Century. <br/><br/>The posh Academy offers up an environment where learning can be fun. Students are</span>
  <span id="freeText12609459725773879722" style="display:none"><b>HOLY FREAKING CLIFFHANGER</b>!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461697152ra/18898985.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am actually happy I put off reading <i>Truly Devious</i> for almost a year after it was released, because honestly, I don't think I could have waited for the sequel.<br><br>Well played, Maureen Johnson. Well played!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484147672ra/21687118.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Ellingham Academy</i>, set in the remote mountains of Vermont, is a private school for gifted students, founded by the wealthy industrialist, Albert Ellingham, at the turn of the 20th Century. <br><br>The posh Academy offers up an environment where learning can be fun. Students are allowed to pursue individual interests with hardly any limits.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548693037ra/26981478.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For Stevie Bell, her number one interest is criminal investigation. After she is accepted to Ellingham, she is anxious to delve into the decades old Truly Devious cold case. <br><br>Shortly after the school was founded, Albert Ellingham's wife and daughter were kidnapped and held for ransom. <br><br>His wife's body was eventually found but his daughter, Alice, was never recovered. Soon thereafter, Albert himself, died under mysterious circumstances.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548693037ra/26981477.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Adjusting to school life is tough for Stevie. She suffers from an anxiety disorder that makes things more challenging for her than it would for a kid who doesn't have the same issues.<br><br>I found this very relatable and thought that the anxiety rep was some of the best I have read in YA; at least based on my own personal experiences. <br><br>I truly (no pun intended) enjoyed the character of Stevie and am very excited that we are getting more books with her as the main protagonist.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548693037ra/26981479.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not only did I relate to Stevie because of her anxiety disorder, but I also am most interested in crime and criminal investigation. I know what it is like for people to find that a little odd, particularly parents. <br><br>My parents grew to support my interests, but as a child, researching and clipping articles on killings, mass murders, cold cases, etc., can seem a little strange. Perhaps that contributed to my love for this book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548693037ra/26981480.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I also found the set-up of the Ellingham kidnappings interesting in that in reminded me of the Lindbergh baby kidnapping in 1932: the wealthy industrialist, he missing child, the ransom and the cryptic notes.<br><br>There were a lot of similarities and I found it easy to follow along with the intrigue because of that. I am curious to know if the author was at all inspired by that case.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591748604ra/29621329.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I just think this was a perfect book for me. <br><br>It catered so well to all of my interests. I loved the cast of characters. The writing was fun and engaging and I cannot wait to pick up <i>The Vanishing Staircase</i>!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12609459725773879722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2623733837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2623733837" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2623733837?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2623733837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12721180794932664345"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A girl from Pittsburgh came to Ellingham Academy and she wanted to see a dead body. She got her wish.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Friends, you’d think a book that is centered around two different murders would be a lot more exciting and enjoyable to read. I know I sound harsh already, but I just really thought I was going to love this one. But I truly only ended up loving the atmosphere of the setting and the amazing anxiety rep. That’s it. <br/><br/>This story stars a young girl named Stevie, who just got invited to at</span>
  <span id="freeText12721180794932664345" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A girl from Pittsburgh came to Ellingham Academy and she wanted to see a dead body. She got her wish.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Friends, you’d think a book that is centered around two different murders would be a lot more exciting and enjoyable to read. I know I sound harsh already, but I just really thought I was going to love this one. But I truly only ended up loving the atmosphere of the setting and the amazing anxiety rep. That’s it. <br /><br />This story stars a young girl named Stevie, who just got invited to attend Ellingham Academy, a very prestigious, private school for the most gifted of children. Stevie has dreamed of being a detective her entire life and feels like this is going to be an amazing new adventure for her, because Ellingham Academy is also well known for a murder mystery that happened years and year ago, which was never solved, and one body was never found. The only thing that was found was a letter signed truly devious, which also quickly was destroyed. <br /><br />Stevie thinks it will be so much fun to investigate the school (which is built into the side of a mountain, like, so freaking cool) but another murder soon happens to a person that she recently befriended. Now, she feels like she must get to the bottom of both of these mysteries, and she’s uncovering more and more secrets that were supposed to be kept hidden. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Schools may be famous for many things: academics, graduates, sports teams. They are not supposed to be famous for murders.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Trust me, I made that synopsis sound way cooler than the actual book. Stevie is a cool character though, and I liked seeing her dynamic with her very conservative parents, when she is in a much more liberal mindset. And as I mentioned in the opening paragraph, Stevie has many anxiety and panic attacks throughout this story, and I honestly have never read a more realistic portrayal of how my attacks actually feel and I am still in awe of it. Like, I completely believe that this has to be an ownvoices portrayal, because it was so expertly crafted. <br /><br />But another fun thing about this book is that we get to see Stevie interact with all the other kids at this private school, and they are all truly possible suspects. Yet, the reader will also be left guessing how this new murder will correlate with the one from the past that was never truly solved. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“When you have enough power and money, you can dictate the meanings of words.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Going into this, everyone told me that the ending was going to kill me and probably make me the third victim of this tale, but honestly? It just annoyed me. Like, it was so far out there that I was just left completely flabbergasted. Especially after Stevie’s discovery prior to that wild ending. I don’t know, I just felt like it actually ended up leaving a bad taste in my mouth, and for sure didn’t make me excited to pick up the next one. <br /><br />Overall, this just wasn’t for me. But please take my review with a grain of salt, because almost everyone I know loves and adores this story. I also think a big reason why this might not have been a hit for me is also because I had just read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448915119" rel="nofollow noopener">A Study in Charlotte</a> and completely fallen in love with that contemporary murder mystery. Maybe I was subconsciously comparing the two? I don’t know, but I just didn’t love this one, friends, even though I really wish that I would have! <br /><br /><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br /><br /><b>Content and trigger warnings</b> for underage drinking, panic attacks, murder, and use of the word cr*zy.<br /><br />Buddy Read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/alexalovesbooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexa</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/41098570-khouloud" rel="nofollow noopener">Khouloud</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13614926-caidyn-semi-hiatus-bw-reviews-he-him-his" rel="nofollow noopener">Caidyn</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13507409-amy" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5376236-bookables" rel="nofollow noopener">Heather</a>! ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="12721180794932664345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7516200784347698539">Love the story, hate the love interest.<br/><br/>I read this book in a single day. Granted, I spent almost 7 hours on a train and had no evening plans so it was just me and the book and no one else for a whole day but I'm not gonna complain. It was a good day, and I say that despite hating spending more than 90 minutes on any mode of transport, be it trains or planes.<br/><br/>I though it was an extremely good start for a mystery series. The setting is exciting as it is a super rich boarding school for the very tal</span>
  <span id="freeText7516200784347698539" style="display:none">Love the story, hate the love interest.<br /><br />I read this book in a single day. Granted, I spent almost 7 hours on a train and had no evening plans so it was just me and the book and no one else for a whole day but I'm not gonna complain. It was a good day, and I say that despite hating spending more than 90 minutes on any mode of transport, be it trains or planes.<br /><br />I though it was an extremely good start for a mystery series. The setting is exciting as it is a super rich boarding school for the very talented and smart in the middle of nowhere, secret tunnels included. There's an unsolved kidnapping and murder from almost 100 years ago, there are new friends and interesting teachers and threatening messages written with cutout letters. The characters were fun apart from the guy the main character is supposed to fall in love with who radiates punch-me-in-the-face-because-I'm-a-dick energy and is as cliché as they come. It was highly entertaining if not gay enough for my liking.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

  <span id="freeText9996477539574532636" style="display:none"><b> Truly devious:- ⭐⭐.15/5<br>Vanishing stair :- ⭐.75/5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3467995395?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener"> Read review here </a><br>Hand on wall :- ⭐⭐.5/5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3469949259" rel="nofollow noopener"> read review here </a></b><br><br>*Spoiler alert*<br><br><br><i>Yeah so oh boy , I just read this renowned, esteemed, honoured and lauded book that everybody was asking me to read when I last wrote in my review to suggest me a good y/a mystery thriller book.<br><br>And please, to people who asked me to read this, just shoo go away you may not be able to Handle this!<br><br> And also the people who haven’t still read this please go away because there are gonna be a lot of spoilers!<br><br>•	There are tons tons of videos/reviews about how good this book is just check them out because it’s a rant and definitely not a place for you!<br><br><b>someone said the book has got some really interesting AGATHA CHRISTIE mentions and you know i love her !<br>there were a total of 6 AC mentions that too totally unrelated! and dont argue with me , i counted okay!</b><br>So back to the <s>rant</s> point:-<br>•	Wtf did I just read , I think my brain just committed suicide and there are still 2 more parts to go!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596023731ra/29876687.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>•	Where do I even start? Well obviously the plot/synopsis!<br>Well the thing about the synopsis was its intriguing and it bluffs you into reading this, its fucking incredible how interesting the synopsis was compared to entire book! <br><br>•<b>	This book was ‘SUPPOSED ‘ to be an mystery thriller and that’s why I was here, congrats you tricked me and I am happy to be clowned for 12345 times this week.</b><br><br>•	By the time I completed the book I was out of fucks I give this book<br><br>•	200 pages into the book and guess what happened ?<br>•	Nothing <br>•	NOTHING EXCEPT<br>•	Building the environment , atmosphere, building the timelines , constantly jumping from timelines and and and<br>•	CHARACTER INTRODUCTION <br>•	<b>I HAVEN'T IN MY ENTIRE LIFE SEEN A BUNCH OF TEENS WITH BORING HOBBIES AND 0 EMOTIONAL DEPTH</b><br>•	They were fucking robots/machinery/machines whatever you wanna call them.<br><br>•	<b>Steive/stephaine</b> :- she is just toooooooooo much ! okay like you are smart,bright,intelligent fine good for you, but can you please use your brain sometime?<br><br>Honestly this book would have ended if Steive would have confessed to Larry finding something which was very imp long ago but no she is SHERLOCK ( and author left no stone unturned for readers to believe that she is sooo smart and whatever she is doing is good)<br>She is introduced to us a someone really good at this , like she could solve the mystery FBI couldn’t solve for past 80 years!<br>Right so you expect her to be good!<br>But she omg ! she really get on my nerves?<br><br>•	She tried really tooooooooooooooo hard to be HERCULE POIROT! And let me tell you girl whatever the hell you were trying to do don’t put it on AGATHA CHRISTIE( she is my love ) , that’s exactly not what hercule poirot do so please just fuck off and play with your boyfriend !<br><br>•	Speaking of boyfriend read this:-<br><br><b>I think her brain was too busy being awesome that she didn’t mind making out in room of a girl who is missing with a boy who might be hiding something without giving a fuck that this room is still not searched !!!!!!</b><br>Dudeeeeeeeee!! Are you out of your mind!<br><br>•	<b>Second imp character DAVID</b> :- SO HE IS PHYSCIOPATH !<br>Like imagine this ,<br><br>Hi I am David and if I have to stup up a person I say “ my parents are dead” though they are alive <br>I do stupid stuff and stare at a girl name steive and asks my rich politician dad to give better jobs to her parents and I think I am cool!<br>I lie a lot , like its my hobby and I love it<br>And yes you could totally trust me!<br><br>•	 Rest there are soo many characters whom its okay if you don’t care about!<br><br><br>•	There was a character named Vi, who is non binary character, I was really happy with this rep but every other time they are mentioned, Vi is mentioned instead of using the pronoun.<br>•	I was so frustrated like idk why ? that put me off.<br>•	And again in the first 20 pages of book, there was a girl wearing hijab and she was never mentioned again, she was just there for diversity rep just like Vi for LGBTQIAP+ rep!<br>•	Immediately those things ……<br>•	Ahhh it was frustrating !<br><br> and that ending i mean wtf ! like what the author expected us to be shocked, intrigued dude please !<br><br>I just care about what happened to ALBERT and his family I don’t give a fuck whatever this steive wanna do with her life !<br><br>So bye!</i></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555916573" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2555916573?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=3-and-a-half-stars">3-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror-etc">mystery-thriller-horror-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=historical">historical</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2555916573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6964162125913949618">JOHN GREEN, PAY ATTENTION. This is how you write a cool mystery-y book with quirky teens without making me want to die.<br/><br/>Okay, John Green, you can stop reading now. I think it would make me uncomfortable if you read the rest of this review, considering <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2088821264?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>the mean things I’ve said</a> and the mean things your fans have said to me in the comments of my mean things. We just have too much backstory.<br/><br/>Now, for the rest of you!<br/><br/>WHAT A FUN RIDE.<br/><br/>As soon as I heard this book was “unsolved murder mystery at boarding</span>
  <span id="freeText6964162125913949618" style="display:none">JOHN GREEN, PAY ATTENTION. This is how you write a cool mystery-y book with quirky teens without making me want to die.<br /><br />Okay, John Green, you can stop reading now. I think it would make me uncomfortable if you read the rest of this review, considering <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2088821264?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">the mean things I’ve said</a> and the mean things your fans have said to me in the comments of my mean things. We just have too much backstory.<br /><br />Now, for the rest of you!<br /><br />WHAT A FUN RIDE.<br /><br />As soon as I heard this book was “unsolved murder mystery at boarding school,” I was in. When I heard the elaboration “unsolved rich people murder mystery from History mixed with current boarding school murder mystery plus true crime aficionado,” I was EXCITED.<br /><br />And whoa mama was that excitement warranted.<br /><br />This was not a perfect read for me by any means. I think the quirkiness was wayyy extraneous at some points (even if it wasn’t John Green-level - but truly what is), and it took away from the pacing and the believability. It kind of felt surreal at times. (Like, can we stop talking about the girl who somehow has her dirty unshowered hair in a million tiny ponytails tied with baby socks and get to the murdering, please?)<br /><br />Also, the pacing of this was weird just because it’s a three-book series with one or two main mysteries. So you get answers at some points in this book, but not a lot of them and not really any that matter. <br /><br />A very unsatisfying experience.<br /><br />I think if I could have read all three books at once and pretended they were one very long book, I would have liked this more. As is, it’s a solid three point five.<br /><br />Also, I already forget what happened in the second book. But that’s unrelated.<br /><br />Bottom line: This was fun and promising! But weird stuff prevented it from being any more than that.<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />baby, let me tell you...I GOT WHAT I CAME FOR.<br /><br />review to come<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />i am ready for INTRIGUE. i am ready for SUSPENSE. i am ready for CRIME and MURDER.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6964162125913949618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText7614811707797119609" style="display:none">Three a little disappointed but still determined enough to give a chance to the second book of trilogy stars. <br /><br />Firstly what I liked about this book:<br />Curiosity didn’t kill the cat but intrigued a dog lover like me, mostly I’m really wondering the correlation between the murders in the past and now! So I want to learn more! The series still keep my attention and last half was real page turner. <br /><br />I always enjoy murder mysteries. I liked references of Christie and Conan Doyle books, methods of solving mysteries. <br /><br />What I didn’t like about the book:<br />The worst character development ever:<br />There are bunch of boring characters who have no emotional depths. <br />Our heroine Stevie reminded me of Riverdale’s Betty Cooper who likes to act like Nancy Drew ( who I also dislike so much). I don’t know the reasons of her panic attacks, her hostility to her parents, her obsession to solve the crimes. Maybe we’ll learn more about her family background on the upcoming books. <br /><br />And David, he is number one asshole, who treated her like trash and we learned that he is manipulating liar! <br />I don’t consider him as a hero of the book because of his short time existence at the parts( and he did nothing heroic ! He was mostly annoying, pretentious douchebag) <br />I also disliked Ellie! Not much idea about Janelle! <br />Only Nate gives me hope, he’s a writer suffering from creativity crisis, he is weird, a little nerd, but he was the most trustworthy one who always supported Stevie! He is my hero candidate! <br /><br />And the ending! I don’t think it was real cliffhanger! It made me more pissed off! If he is a real person, I’ll punch David on the face! I wish the ending would be a big revelation or clue about one of the murders !<br /><br />Well at least there are good reviews about the second book! I’ll keep reading and hoping to see more layered character development, twists, surprises and big revelations!<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>

<div id="review_2741259183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2741259183" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2741259183?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=thriller-crime">thriller-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2741259183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9168222683983970400">I have come to the conclusion that murder-mysteries that <i>aren't standalones and therefore don't wrap up in one book</i> are very stressful. I have QUESTIONS and no answers and also no sequel in my cold clammy paws. Dammit, universe.<br/><br/><b>Anyway this was my first time reading a solo book by Maureen Johnson!</b> I definitely enjoyed this! I read her short story in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33290383.Let_it_Snow' title='Let it Snow by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Let it Snow</a> and can 100% confirm that I remember nothing because it was like, um, 4 years ago that I read it. Anyway this reminded me a ton of John G</span>
  <span id="freeText9168222683983970400" style="display:none">I have come to the conclusion that murder-mysteries that <i>aren't standalones and therefore don't wrap up in one book</i> are very stressful. I have QUESTIONS and no answers and also no sequel in my cold clammy paws. Dammit, universe.<br /><br /><b>Anyway this was my first time reading a solo book by Maureen Johnson!</b> I definitely enjoyed this! I read her short story in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33290383.Let_it_Snow" title="Let it Snow by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Let it Snow</a> and can 100% confirm that I remember nothing because it was like, um, 4 years ago that I read it. Anyway this reminded me a ton of John Green's style with the absolutely bizarrely quirky characters who are entirely endearing very fast.<br /><br /><b>I loved Stevie!</b> I'm not entirely convinced she's not somewhat autistic (lol we autistics can spy each other ok) and she was very intense and focused and also awkward and vulnerable? She's obsessed with murder mysteries, specifically solving the cold case of the new boarding school she's going to. I also loved how dearly she wanted friends but how hard she found it not to accidentally isolate herself?! Like relate.<br /><br />Also the secondary characters were so wild and also thoroughly awesome. I loved Nate (the genius fantasy writer who can no longer write and absolutely will have a meltdown if asked about writing) and Ellie was fascinating (the artist who grew up in a commune and dyes her skirt and self pink in a bath and drinks a lot) and David was interesting (a shabby mysterious boy who compulsively lies and flirts with Stevie but is definitely Not Saying Everything). I wanted more from Janelle but she kinda faded in the second half?<br /><br /><b>Also there is MURDER.</b> And I have so many questions. I kind of got lost with the backstory scenes for the 1930s cold case mystery because there were a lot of males with old fashioned names and like ...ya, I'm lost. But I was like holding mY BREATH waiting for Stevie to put clues together. And I love how she totally has a Sherlock Holmes vibe but she's not unrealistically genius, so still super relatable.<br /><br /><b>Basically I solidly loved this.</b> It just felt really refreshing and the writing was addictive and funny and had so much voice. I solidly regret not having read more from Maureen Johnson earlier, ok?! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9168222683983970400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2607733996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2607733996" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2607733996?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of A Study in Charlotte</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=starred-2018">starred-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mysteries-thrillers-horror">mysteries-thrillers-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=1">1</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2607733996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14167298721768850441"><b>Updated</b><br/><br/>So I've performed a fit of astonishing perseverance and read the whole book. Was it worth the effort? Not really, but I am at least ready to discuss details with my book club mates.<br/><br/>It's not that this novel is bad. I don't think it is. It's an ok mystery, with historical flashbacks that are much more compelling than present day obnoxious kids mucking about. But it's just so very boring. The main character is boring, the students are precocious and boring, they talk about boring things and </span>
  <span id="freeText14167298721768850441" style="display:none"><b>Updated</b><br /><br />So I've performed a fit of astonishing perseverance and read the whole book. Was it worth the effort? Not really, but I am at least ready to discuss details with my book club mates.<br /><br />It's not that this novel is bad. I don't think it is. It's an ok mystery, with historical flashbacks that are much more compelling than present day obnoxious kids mucking about. But it's just so very boring. The main character is boring, the students are precocious and boring, they talk about boring things and they even romance each other in the most boring ways. <br /><br />This is a case of personal taste though, and nothing else. Some authors just can't entertain me no matter what. Jenny Han, Victoria Schwab and yes, Maureen Johnson.<br /><br />What is objectively annoying about this book though, is the ending, which there is none. What's the point of reading the whole mystery book to just find out that you don't even have all basic facts to guess the murderer? <br /><br />Waste of time.<br /><br /><b>Original hot take</b><br /><br />Can a book bore you to death within one page? Yes, it can.<br /><br />I did listen to about an hour of it on audio anyway, but there is just nothing compelling in this story for me. Zero. Which, to be fair, I can say about every Maureen Johnson work I've ever read. Clearly we should part our ways forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14167298721768850441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14352839733684731627">3.5 Stars<br/><br/>I don't think I'm suppose to like this book. I mean I should like it and I did like it but I don't know why I liked it. <br/><br/>The plot sounds great Stevie is a True Crime fanatic (something we share in common) who's bookcase is filled with the great detective novels, such as Sherlock and Poirot. She listens to True Crime podcast and is obsessed with the ID channel (again something we share in common) and hopes to become an FBI agent when she grows up. Stevie applies to and is accepted into El</span>
  <span id="freeText14352839733684731627" style="display:none">3.5 Stars<br /><br />I don't think I'm suppose to like this book. I mean I should like it and I did like it but I don't know why I liked it. <br /><br />The plot sounds great Stevie is a True Crime fanatic (something we share in common) who's bookcase is filled with the great detective novels, such as Sherlock and Poirot. She listens to True Crime podcast and is obsessed with the ID channel (again something we share in common) and hopes to become an FBI agent when she grows up. Stevie applies to and is accepted into Ellington an exclusive private school with an infamous past. Stevie sets out to solve the mystery. <br /><br />That sounds like a great premise and it is but nothing really happens. We meet what felt like every student at the school(its a lot of people) and we get glimpses of the investigation into the mystery that surrounds the school and we get a brand new mystery that Stevie also investigates. It felt like both mysteries were B-Plots though. Truly Devious spends way more time on teen angst then on the murder mysteries that the book is allegedly about. <br /><br />I know what you're thinking<br /><br /> It sounds like you hated this book, then why the 3.5 star rating? <br /><br />Because Truly Devious was fun! <br /><br />I never for one second thought about putting this book down. I enjoyed reading it. I got caught up in the atmosphere of Ellington Academy and I found Stevie's battle with anxiety completely believable. I have never suffered from anxiety but my mother did and sister does. The way Stevie described how an anxiety or panic attack feels is the way they described them. So for that alone I really enjoyed reading this book. <br /><br />Also the ending was great and I can't wait to read book 2. Since I have such conflicted feelings about this book I won't make any recommendations.<br /><br />Around the Year in 52 Books: A book Featuring a Murder.</span>

<div id="review_2808559521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2808559521" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2808559521?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2808559521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10925496882956865405">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>Stevie Bell has always been a bit different than her peers, much to her parents' chagrin. Much of her childhood and teenage years have been spent feeding her obsession with true crime and mysteries. Her parents wanted her to do the things "normal" teenagers do—hang out with friends, participate in extracurricular activities, maybe even date. But what Stevie wants more than anything is to solve crimes, to one day be as revered as some of the legendary detectives she loves reading about.</span>
  <span id="freeText10925496882956865405" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />Stevie Bell has always been a bit different than her peers, much to her parents' chagrin. Much of her childhood and teenage years have been spent feeding her obsession with true crime and mysteries. Her parents wanted her to do the things "normal" teenagers do—hang out with friends, participate in extracurricular activities, maybe even date. But what Stevie wants more than anything is to solve crimes, to one day be as revered as some of the legendary detectives she loves reading about.<br /><br />When she learns about Ellingham Academy, a prestigious private school in Vermont, she is absolutely desperate to attend. Not only does Ellingham essentially design each student's curriculum around their own interests, but back in the 1930s, the Academy was the scene of one of the most notorious mysteries and unsolved crimes ever. The wife and young daughter of the Academy's wealthy founder were kidnapped and the kidnappers demanded hundreds of thousands of dollars from Ellingham, but he never got his family back. The only clue to the kidnapping was a ransom note in the form of a mocking poem, signed by "Truly Devious."<br /><br />Stevie wants to solve this mystery once and for all, and her passion for doing so is the criteria that gets her admitted to Ellingham. But even though she has a real purpose, and attends a school that supports that purpose, adjustment isn't as easy as she had hoped. She's never really made friends before, and isn't sure of what to make of her eccentric and creative dorm-mates, including a scientist and inventor, a popular and handsome web-series actor, a novelist, an artist with a penchant for alcohol and the saxophone, and David, a coder, who seemed to get under Stevie's skin from the moment they met. <br /><br />One night, when she is participating in the filming of a web series about the kidnapping, it appears that "Truly Devious" has returned to the scene of their original crime, when Stevie sees another mocking ransom note. Not long after, someone is found dead—but did they fall prey to an accident, or was it murder? And is the murderer one of her classmates? Despite being warned about playing detective, that is exactly what Stevie does. But along the way she needs to realize that what she discovers may not make her a hero among her peers as she always imagined it would—and it could threaten the future of the school, or at least her enrollment. Is solving the crime worth the potential damage to the one place she finally feels she fits in?<br /><br />Maureen Johnson's <b>
  <i>Truly Devious</i>
</b> is truly terrific. It's a great read, full of really interesting characters, a dynamic setting, and a compelling mystery that definitely hooked me from the start. I love how the book shifted between the present day and the original kidnapping back in the 1930s, and looked at the way that case unfolded. Ellingham seems like the perfect place to go to school, and I wish a place like that existed when I was younger! (Without the murders and stuff.)<br /><br />Johnson is a great storyteller. Her use of imagery was so evocative and I could picture the Academy in both past and present. She is also tremendously skilled at creating tension between characters and situations—I really wasn't sure whom to trust and it's rare that I feel that way when reading these books. I also liked the way she had diverse characters without making a big deal out of them; it was just matter-of-fact.<br /><br />This is the first book in a series, so the ending was a bit of a confusing cliffhanger, but you can bet I'll be picking up the next book, <b>
  <i>The Vanishing Stair</i>
</b>. I really thought this was a lot of fun, and a great read. <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2018 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html</a>. <br /><br />You can follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10925496882956865405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13094266802723503269" style="display:none"><b>a main character bold enough to knock herself unconscious when her anxiety gets to be too much</b><br /><br />this book was much better than i was expecting, thank the fucking lord. i've read a couple of maureen johnson's other books and haven't ever been very impressed. this one kind of changed my mind about her.<br /><br />basic premise is that a wealthy 1930s tycoon starts a free school for children in the mountains of vermont where he also hosts small but lavish gatherings with the rich and famous. said tycoon's wife and child are kidnapped. present day true crime lover stevie gets into this free school for kids and decides to solve the mystery.<br /><br />but it's not really that simple. stevie is <b>a little uh... weird</b> and she has to contend with the other strange characters in this boarding school as she tries to uncover what happened so many years ago. oh yeah, and one of her classmates happens to get murdered. no biggie.<br /><br />i thought the plot of this was pretty excellent. <b>i definitely wasn't expecting there to be so much focus on stevie's interactions with the other students and her burgeoning hormonal feelings</b> but it didn't take away from her sleuthing too much imo. i liked that there were scenes from 1936 interspersed throughout the story along with police interviews from tycoon's fascinating friends. and i like that the present day murder is still unsolved, along with the past mystery.<br /><br />the only thing that i didn't love, actually (lol wow that's bad shhh), was stevie herself. i understood her single minded obsession pretty well but her contempt for her parents was pretty hard to believe. also her complete lack of personal boundaries and lack of empathy sort of has me wondering if she has mental health issues beyond just anxiety.<br /><br />but that being said, i'm really really curious to see where the next book takes us. i'll definitely be reading it.<br /><br /><b>ps if you felt the charlotte holmes series was lacking in actual mystery you might find this one more satisfying</b><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2662398189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15207543770182082620">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/01/17/truly-devious-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/><b> Actual Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/> <i>“You have to take things as they are, not how you hear they’re supposed to be.”</i><br/><br/>🌟 I usually read contemporaries or mystery/ thriller novels when I want to take a break from the Fantasy genre! This was like 60% Mystery and 40% Contemporary and I am not sure if that was a good combination.<br/><br/>🌟 The writing style was good, not too poetic, not too bland! It was right for a story of this kind. I think w</span>
  <span id="freeText15207543770182082620" style="display:none">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/01/17/truly-devious-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /><b> Actual Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><br /> <i>“You have to take things as they are, not how you hear they’re supposed to be.”</i><br /><br />🌟 I usually read contemporaries or mystery/ thriller novels when I want to take a break from the Fantasy genre! This was like 60% Mystery and 40% Contemporary and I am not sure if that was a good combination.<br /><br />🌟 The writing style was good, not too poetic, not too bland! It was right for a story of this kind. I think what the author was trying to achieve here is to show us the writing process for a mystery kind of novel which is something I appreciate as I am trying to learn more about writing.<br /><br /> <i>“When you have enough power and money, you can dictate the meanings of words.” </i><br /><br />🌟 The idea seems interesting because it is a school for the brightest thinkers, inventors, and artists according to the synopsis! I expected the mystery part to be a little bit better to be honest.<br /><br />🌟 The characters are mediocre in my opinion. I wasn’t a big fan of any of them. I expected to have more mature and smart characters from my imagination of what this could be. Like the characters in Death Note for example!<br /><br />🌟 The author looks like a big fan of Agatha Christie and Sherlock Holmes! I loved the Agatha references but since the author is well versed in those stories, she should know that a huge part of their success is because they are fast, short and to the point. The mystery in this book does not happen until after half of the book and it is not even solved!<br /><br />🌟 I also left reading this closer to the release date of the second book because many said that the cliffhanger was good and they can’t wait! I expected something more from all the hype tbh!<br /><br />🌟 Summary: Reading this book was a strange experience, not much happened as I expected to for a mystery novel, but it was intriguing at the same time that I finished it quite fast. Maybe I prefer short, fast reads as Agatha’s books and I don’t know why this is a trilogy too?! I will continue book 2 but will go with different expectations!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2183834701" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3349689042411757818">I love Maureen Johnson. Truly. And I thought this book was fast-paced, captivating and overall exciting and entertaining. <br/><br/>But. I'm either an idiot, a complete jerk, or possibly both, because this bugs me: a character is referred to as "Truly Devious" based on a letter which was 'signed' "Truly, Devious". This makes me think that "Truly" was the closing (in lieu of "Sincerely") and "Devious" was the writer, so the character would just be "Devious" or perhaps a tongue-in-cheek "Truly, Devious". Ma</span>
  <span id="freeText3349689042411757818" style="display:none">I love Maureen Johnson. Truly. And I thought this book was fast-paced, captivating and overall exciting and entertaining. <br /><br />But. I'm either an idiot, a complete jerk, or possibly both, because this bugs me: a character is referred to as "Truly Devious" based on a letter which was 'signed' "Truly, Devious". This makes me think that "Truly" was the closing (in lieu of "Sincerely") and "Devious" was the writer, so the character would just be "Devious" or perhaps a tongue-in-cheek "Truly, Devious". Maybe it is part of the story that I missed or is yet to come, or (as previously stated) I'm just an annoying reader.<br /><br />I'm still all-on-board for the sequel and I really and truly do love Maureen Johnson.</span>

<div id="review_2353849839" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2353849839" />
    <a title="Alaina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50620706-alaina"><img alt="Alaina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451325817p2/50620706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2353849839?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alaina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alaina" href="/user/show/50620706-alaina">Alaina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=may-challenge-2018">may-challenge-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2353849839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15707860116854513350"><b>I HATE CLIFFHANGERS PEOPLE!</b><br/><br/>So when I went to the bookstore and saw this book I didn't even second guess when it landed in my hands and I handed over money like a robot buying books. It's like I woke up from my haze the next day and had no idea how many books I bought. I should probably stay away from book stores.. but we all know that would never happen. I might die!<br/><br/>Okay so the beginning of <i>Truly Devious</i> was truly amazing. I was hooked instantly. It reminded me of so many previous books, movies,</span>
  <span id="freeText15707860116854513350" style="display:none"><b>I HATE CLIFFHANGERS PEOPLE!</b><br /><br />So when I went to the bookstore and saw this book I didn't even second guess when it landed in my hands and I handed over money like a robot buying books. It's like I woke up from my haze the next day and had no idea how many books I bought. I should probably stay away from book stores.. but we all know that would never happen. I might die!<br /><br />Okay so the beginning of <i>Truly Devious</i> was truly amazing. I was hooked instantly. It reminded me of so many previous books, movies, and shows and that's probably why I enjoyed it so much. The setting and the characters were pretty interesting and definitely kept me turning the pages. However, I definitely developed a ton of questions while reading this book.. and I feel like I didn't really the answers I was hoping for. I'm kind of pissed that I have to wait for the next book to see if I even get a glimpse of those answers.<br /><br />Speaking of characters, I loved Dottie, Stevie, and Nate. Dottie was a favorite at the beginning. Stevie was interesting. Then Nate was probably my favorite of them all. He was completely likable and relatable. I loved him so much. Now even though I liked these characters.. I still feel like I didn't really know them that well. I don't know.. it's probably weird. Just go with it.<br /><br />Then this book shoved so much mystery down my throat. People ending up dead basically everywhere and I instantly stopped trusting every damn character in this book. I just wanted to know who was killing people and if or when the next victim will show up. I felt like I was on a whirlwind mystery never ending roller coaster and I wanted off. I wanted answers people! <br /><br />Overall, it was an interesting book and definitely a page turner. It also had some flaws - like boring parts or the uneven pacing throughout the book. I will most definitely be getting the second book of this series. I need answers and I'm determined to find everything out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15707860116854513350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3091086064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3091086064" />
    <a title="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102159719-reading-tam-ishly"><img alt="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578580640p2/102159719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3091086064?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" href="/user/show/102159719-reading-tam-ishly">Reading_ Tam_ Ishly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3091086064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7603200552715815118">***want to binge read something good? This trilogy is perfect 😘<br/><br/>Picked up this one like two or three times before, it's interesting and all that. Somehow I am not a big mystery reader and I thought that the book would go on forever. And then I thought the anxiety issues and the panic attacks of the main character weren't handled well when it comes to the attitude of the adult characters towards these.<br/>The first half is a bit too slow for me.<br/>Other than that, this was a perfect read. <br/><br/>I absolutely lo</span>
  <span id="freeText7603200552715815118" style="display:none">***want to binge read something good? This trilogy is perfect 😘<br /><br />Picked up this one like two or three times before, it's interesting and all that. Somehow I am not a big mystery reader and I thought that the book would go on forever. And then I thought the anxiety issues and the panic attacks of the main character weren't handled well when it comes to the attitude of the adult characters towards these.<br />The first half is a bit too slow for me.<br />Other than that, this was a perfect read. <br /><br />I absolutely loved the characters, my most favourite being Nate! Ah, he's so damn precious. I would love to steal all his T-shirts someday and we know why.<br />The characters are interesting. A few are plain obnoxious; most of them are quirky, nerdy and geeky...and my most fav kinds😘<br />The atmosphere of the story is not that spooky or dark even if it's all about solving an 80 year old murder mystery. Somehow it just pulla you in and yes, you cannot go back to your normal life until you finish up all the three books. (I am just taking a break to write this unorderly, short review while reading book 2.) <br />Yes, the writing style, the plot, the weird characters and the cliffhangers: EVERYTHING works for this one. And you will never find yourself that happy as when you start immediately the second book. Damn, the second book is going so good!<br /><br />Ah, another thing I didn't like. The unwelcomed romance. Nah. It just didn't work for me. Too insta. Too impulsive. Too not needed at this point. Too out of place. <br /><br />But the first book is good nevertheless. <br /><br />It's the humour parts here and there that keeps me going on, especially when Nate is there. Damn, he's my nerd😘<br /><br />(...and this is why I fail miserably at writing reviews for thrillers and mystery books😁)</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2134505440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10823521784991414162"><i>I received an advanced reader copy via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review</i><br/><br/>WHAT DID I JUST READ?! How did that ending happen? Vague answers, hints at something conclusive, but left with almost...nothing? I’m so confused and kind of pissed off. What did I just read? Was I truly waiting for a semi-decent conclusion when all I got was a “to be continued”? I get that it’s the first in a series, but seriously, what the actual living f*%# did I read? At least give us a decent conclusion! <br/><br/>The bui</span>
  <span id="freeText10823521784991414162" style="display:none"><i>I received an advanced reader copy via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review</i><br /><br />WHAT DID I JUST READ?! How did that ending happen? Vague answers, hints at something conclusive, but left with almost...nothing? I’m so confused and kind of pissed off. What did I just read? Was I truly waiting for a semi-decent conclusion when all I got was a “to be continued”? I get that it’s the first in a series, but seriously, what the actual living f*%# did I read? At least give us a decent conclusion! <br /><br />The build up was good and the main character had her intriguing oddities, but that conclusion knocked down my rating because wtf. I feel so cheated. I feel so damn cheated right now. I feel like this book—this whole series—could have been finished in a couple of more chapters. Man. I’m going to bed, I don’t have any more patience for this. <br /><br />Happy reading! </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3+PNTIKhEch///pDyUkD8nRqSBxpe6Qni7c0kH8Ve8HZhtw8sKrgUgsC7KHoRKQh3glRoPl1jtwP+HpQWB4Zmw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AHwt8M1v52tjz7JvLNgOo6egGuqE+IYihPaYRJYo4xUGGTyA/2QW8RcypI0N1alwDcMDVhT2rNkAudaEsSOBTw==')})
  }

But the path to the truth has more twists and turns than she can imagine—and moving forward involves hurting someone she cares for.
